It is exacerbated by excessive, misdirected or obtrusive uses of light, but even carefully used light fundamentally alters natural conditions. As a major side-effect of urbanization, it is blamed for compromising health, disrupting ecosystems and spoiling aesthetic environments.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input href="#Reduction_of_natural_sky_polarization"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Reduction of natural sky polarization</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Reduction"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Reduction</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Improving_lighting_fixtures"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Improving lighting fixtures</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Adjusting_types_of_light_sources"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Adjusting types of light sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Re-designing_lighting_plans"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Re-designing lighting plans</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Light <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> is the adding-of/added light itself, in analogy to added sound, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, etc. Adverse consequences are multiple; some of them may not be known yet. Scientific definitions thus include the following:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The degradation of photic habitat by artificial light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scientific_definition1985_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-scientific_definition1985-1">[1]</a></sup></li>\n<li>The alteration of natural light levels in the outdoor environment owing to artificial light sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scientific_definition0_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-scientific_definition0-2">[2]</a></sup></li>\n<li>The alteration of light levels in the outdoor environment (from those present naturally) due to man-made sources of light. Indoor light pollution is such alteration of light levels in the indoor environment due to sources of light, which compromises human health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scientific_definition_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-scientific_definition-3">[3]</a></sup></li>\n<li>The introduction by humans, directly or indirectly, of artificial light into the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scientific_definitionAct_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-scientific_definitionAct-4">[4]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The first three of the above four scientific definitions describe the state of the environment. The fourth (and newest) one describes the process of polluting by light.\n</p><p>Light pollution competes with starlight in the <a href="/wiki/Night_sky" title="Night sky">night sky</a> for urban residents, interferes with <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomical</a> <a href="/wiki/Observatory" title="Observatory">observatories</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and, like any other form of <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>, disrupts <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> and has adverse health effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Light pollution is a side-effect of industrial civilization. Its sources include building exterior and interior lighting, advertising, outdoor area lighting (e.g. car parks/parking lots), offices, factories, streetlights, and illuminated sporting venues. It is most severe in highly industrialized, densely populated areas of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and in major cities in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> like <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, but even relatively small amounts of light can be noticed and create problems. Awareness of the deleterious effects of light pollution began early in the 20th Century (see e.g. Beston<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>), but efforts to address effects did not begin until the 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In the 1980s a global <a href="/wiki/Dark-sky_movement" title="Dark-sky movement">dark-sky movement</a> emerged with the founding of the <a href="/wiki/International_Dark-Sky_Association" title="International Dark-Sky Association">International Dark-Sky Association</a> (IDA). There are now such educational and advocacy organizations in many countries worldwide.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_on_energy_usage">Impact on energy usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Impact on energy usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Energy_conservation" title="Energy conservation">Energy conservation</a> advocates contend that light pollution must be addressed by changing the <a href="/wiki/Habituation" title="Habituation">habits</a> of society, so that lighting is used more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lighting_efficiency" title="Lighting efficiency">efficiently</a>, with less waste and less creation of unwanted or unneeded illumination.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Several industry groups also recognize light pollution as an important issue. For example, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Institution_of_Lighting_Engineers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Institution of Lighting Engineers (page does not exist)">Institution of Lighting Engineers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> provides its members with information about light pollution, the problems it causes, and how to reduce its impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Although, recent research<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> point that the energy efficiency is not enough to reduce the light pollution because of the <a href="/wiki/Rebound_effect_(conservation)" title="Rebound effect (conservation)">rebound effect</a>.\n</p><p>Since not everyone is irritated by the same lighting sources, it is common for one person\'s light "pollution" to be light that is desirable for another. One example of this is found in advertising, when an advertiser wishes for particular lights to be bright and visible, even though others find them annoying. Other types of light pollution are more certain. For instance, light that <i>accidentally</i> crosses a property boundary and annoys a neighbor is generally wasted and pollutive light.\n</p><p>Disputes are still common when deciding appropriate action; and differences in opinion over what light is considered reasonable, and who should be responsible, mean that negotiation must sometimes take place between parties. Where objective measurement is desired, light levels can be quantified by field measurement or <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_model" title="Mathematical model">mathematical modeling</a>, with results typically displayed as an isophote map or light <a href="/wiki/Contour_line" title="Contour line">contour map</a>. Authorities have also taken a variety of measures for dealing with light pollution, depending on the interests, beliefs and understandings of the society involved.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Measures range from doing nothing at all, to implementing strict laws and regulations about how lights may be installed and used.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/22/Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg/200px-Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/22/Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg/300px-Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/22/Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg/400px-Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skybeamer-uniqema-640.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A light pollution source, using a broad spectrum <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_halide_lamp" title="Metal halide lamp">metal halide lamp</a>, pointing upward at Uniqema factory, <a href="/wiki/Gouda,_South_Holland" title="Gouda, South Holland">Gouda</a>, the Netherlands.</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Light pollution</b> is caused by inefficient, unappealing, or (arguably) unnecessary use of artificial light. Specific categories of light pollution include light trespass, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over-illumination" title="Over-illumination">over-illumination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glare_(vision)" title="Glare (vision)">glare</a>, light clutter, and <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a>. A single offending light source often falls into more than one of these categories.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Light_trespass">Light trespass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Light trespass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Light trespass occurs when unwanted light enters one\'s property, for instance, by shining over a neighbor\'s fence. A common light trespass problem occurs when a strong light enters the window of one\'s home from the outside, causing problems such as <a href="/wiki/Sleep_deprivation" title="Sleep deprivation">sleep deprivation</a>. A number of cities in the U.S. have developed standards for outdoor lighting to protect the rights of their citizens against light trespass. To assist them, the <a href="/wiki/International_Dark-Sky_Association" title="International Dark-Sky Association">International Dark-Sky Association</a> has developed a set of model lighting ordinances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_Dark-Sky_Association_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-International_Dark-Sky_Association-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dark-Sky Association was started to reduce the light going up into the sky which reduces visibility of stars (see Skyglow below). This is any light which is emitted more than 90&#176; above <a href="/wiki/Nadir" title="Nadir">nadir</a>. By limiting light at this 90&#176; mark they have also reduced the light output in the 80&#8211;90&#176; range which creates most of the light trespass issues.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg/220px-Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg/330px-Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg/440px-Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Lights_from_afar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The light pollution from the city of Phoenix can be seen from 55 miles away in Surprise.  Even from afar the pollution is severe and travels high into the night sky.</div></div></div>\n<p>U.S. federal agencies may also enforce standards and process complaints within their areas of jurisdiction. For instance, in the case of light trespass by white <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strobe" title="Strobe">strobe</a> lighting from communication towers in excess of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> minimum lighting requirements<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> maintains an Antenna Structure Registration database<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCC_Antenna_Structure_Registration_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCC_Antenna_Structure_Registration-14">[14]</a></sup> information which citizens may use to identify offending structures and provides a mechanism for processing citizen inquiries and complaints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcc.gov_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcc.gov-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Green_Building_Council" title="U.S. Green Building Council">U.S. Green Building Council</a> (USGBC) has also incorporated a credit for reducing the amount of light trespass and sky glow into their environmentally friendly building standard known as <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a>.\n</p><p>Light trespass can be reduced by selecting light fixtures which limit the amount of light emitted more than 80&#176; above the nadir. The <a href="/wiki/Illuminating_Engineering_Society_of_North_America" title="Illuminating Engineering Society of North America">IESNA</a> definitions include full cutoff (0%), cutoff (10%), and semi-cutoff (20%). (These definitions also include limits on light emitted above 90&#176; to reduce sky glow.)\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Over-illumination">Over-illumination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Over-illumination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over-illumination" title="Over-illumination">Over-illumination</a></div>\n<table class="box-Bad_summary plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-bad-summary" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>may not properly <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Summary_style" title="Wikipedia:Summary style">summarize</a> its corresponding main article</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit">help improve it</a> by rewriting it in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Encyclopedic_style" title="Wikipedia:Encyclopedic style">encyclopedic style</a>.</span><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HPS-lamps.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/HPS-lamps.jpg/190px-HPS-lamps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/HPS-lamps.jpg/285px-HPS-lamps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/HPS-lamps.jpg/380px-HPS-lamps.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HPS-lamps.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An office building is illuminated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sodium_lamp" title="Sodium lamp">high pressure sodium (HPS)</a> lamps shining upward, of which much light goes into the sky and neighboring apartment blocks and causes light pollution.</div></div></div>\n<p>Over-illumination is the excessive use of light. Specifically within the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, over-illumination is responsible for approximately two million <a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)#Oil_barrel" title="Barrel (unit)">barrels of oil</a> per day in <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy wasted</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This is based upon U.S. consumption of equivalent of 18.8 million barrels per day (2,990,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of petroleum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Explained_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Explained-16">[16]</a></sup> It is further noted in the same U.S. Department of Energy source that over 30% of all primary energy is consumed by commercial, industrial and residential sectors. Energy audits of existing buildings demonstrate that the lighting component of residential, commercial and industrial uses consumes about 20&#8211;40% of those land uses, variable with region and land use. (Residential use lighting consumes only 10&#8211;30% of the energy bill while commercial buildings\' major use is lighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irby_Circuit_&#8211;_Energy_Savings_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irby_Circuit_&#8211;_Energy_Savings-17">[17]</a></sup>) Thus lighting energy accounts for about four or five million barrels of oil (equivalent) per day. Again energy audit data demonstrates that about 30&#8211;60% of energy consumed in lighting is unneeded or gratuitous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An alternative calculation starts with the fact that commercial building lighting consumes in excess of 81.68 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terawatt" title="Terawatt">terawatts</a> (1999 data) of electricity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eia.doe.gov_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-eia.doe.gov-19">[19]</a></sup> according to the U.S. DOE. Thus commercial lighting alone consumes about four to five million barrels per day (equivalent) of petroleum, in line with the alternate rationale above to estimate U.S. lighting energy consumption. Even among developed countries there are large differences in patterns of light use. American cities emit 3&#8211;5 times more light to space per capita compared to German cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over-illumination stems from several factors:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Consensus based standards or norms that are not based on vision science;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Not using timers, <a href="/wiki/Occupancy_sensor" title="Occupancy sensor">occupancy sensors</a> or other controls to extinguish lighting when not needed;</li>\n<li>Improper design, by specifying higher levels of light than needed for a given visual task;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EcoSky_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-EcoSky-22">[22]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Incorrect choice of fixtures or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_bulbs" title="Light bulbs">light bulbs</a>, which do not direct light into areas as needed;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EcoSky_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-EcoSky-22">[22]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Improper selection of hardware to utilize more energy than needed to accomplish the lighting task;</li>\n<li>Incomplete training of building managers and occupants to use lighting systems efficiently;</li>\n<li>Inadequate lighting maintenance resulting in increased <a href="/wiki/Stray_light" title="Stray light">stray light</a> and energy costs;</li>\n<li>"Daylight lighting" demanded by citizens to reduce crime or by shop owners to attract customers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-23">[23]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Substitution of old lamps with more efficient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LED" title="LED">LEDs</a> using the same electrical power; and</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_lighting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Indirect lighting (page does not exist)">Indirect lighting</a> techniques, such as illuminating a vertical wall to bounce light onto the ground.</li></ul>\n<p>Most of these issues can be readily corrected with available, inexpensive technology, and with resolution of landlord/tenant practices that create barriers to rapid correction of these matters. Most importantly, public awareness would need to improve for industrialized countries to realize the large payoff in reducing over-illumination.\n</p><p>In certain cases an over-illumination lighting technique may be needed. For example, indirect lighting is often used to obtain a "softer" look, since hard direct lighting is generally found less desirable for certain surfaces, such as skin. The indirect lighting method is perceived as more cozy and suits bars, restaurants and living quarters. It is also possible to block the direct lighting effect by adding softening filters or other solutions, though intensity will be reduced.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glare">Glare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Glare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Glare_(vision)" title="Glare (vision)">Glare (vision)</a></div>\n<p>Glare can be categorized into different types. One such classification is described in a book by Bob Mizon, coordinator for the British Astronomical Association\'s Campaign for Dark Skies, as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mizon,_Bob_2001_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mizon,_Bob_2001-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Blinding glare</i> describes effects such as that caused by staring into the Sun. It is completely blinding and leaves temporary or permanent vision deficiencies.</li>\n<li><i>Disability glare</i> describes effects such as being blinded by oncoming car lights, or light scattering in fog or in the eye, reducing contrast, as well as reflections from print and other dark areas that render them bright, with significant reduction in sight capabilities.</li>\n<li><i>Discomfort glare</i> does not typically cause a dangerous situation in itself, though it is annoying and irritating at best. It can potentially cause fatigue if experienced over extended periods.</li></ul>\n<p>According to Mario Motta, president of the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Medical_Society" title="Massachusetts Medical Society">Massachusetts Medical Society</a>, "... glare from bad lighting is a public-health hazard&#8212;especially the older you become. Glare light scattering in the eye causes loss of contrast and leads to unsafe driving conditions, much like the glare on a dirty windshield from low-angle sunlight or the high beams from an oncoming car."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MottaJune09_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-MottaJune09-25">[25]</a></sup> In essence bright and/or badly shielded lights around roads can partially blind drivers or pedestrians and contribute to accidents.\n</p><p>The blinding effect is caused in large part by reduced contrast due to light scattering in the eye by excessive brightness, or to reflection of light from dark areas in the field of vision, with luminance similar to the background luminance. This kind of glare is a particular instance of disability glare, called veiling glare. (This is not the same as loss of accommodation of <a href="/wiki/Night_vision" title="Night vision">night vision</a> which is caused by the direct effect of the light itself on the eye.)\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg/220px-San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg/330px-San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg/440px-San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Tan_Mountain_Lights.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The view of the Phoenix metro area and its light clutter and pollution from the top of Goldmine Trail in the San Tan Mountains.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Light_clutter">Light clutter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Light clutter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Las_Vegas_Strip.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="1744" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Las_Vegas_Strip.png/200px-Las_Vegas_Strip.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Las_Vegas_Strip.png/300px-Las_Vegas_Strip.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Las_Vegas_Strip.png/400px-Las_Vegas_Strip.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Las_Vegas_Strip.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a> displays excessive groupings of colorful lights. This is a classic example of light clutter.</div></div></div>\n<p>Light clutter refers to excessive groupings of lights. Groupings of lights may generate confusion, distract from obstacles (including those that they may be intended to illuminate), and potentially cause accidents. Clutter is particularly noticeable on roads where the street lights are badly designed, or where brightly lit advertising surrounds the roadways. Depending on the motives of the person or organization that installed the lights, their placement and design can even be intended to distract drivers, and can contribute to accidents.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurement_and_global_effects">Measurement and global effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Measurement and global effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Light_pollution_europe.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Light_pollution_europe.jpg/200px-Light_pollution_europe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Light_pollution_europe.jpg/300px-Light_pollution_europe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Light_pollution_europe.jpg/400px-Light_pollution_europe.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Light_pollution_europe.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>False colors show intensities of <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a> from artificial light sources.</div></div></div>\n<p>Measuring the effect of sky glow on a global scale is a complex procedure. The natural atmosphere is not completely dark, even in the absence of terrestrial sources of light and illumination from the Moon. This is caused by two main sources: <i>airglow</i> and <i>scattered light</i>.\n</p><p>At high altitudes, primarily above the <a href="/wiki/Mesosphere" title="Mesosphere">mesosphere</a>, there is enough UV radiation from the sun of very short wavelength to cause <a href="/wiki/Ionization" title="Ionization">ionization</a>. When the ions collide with electrically neutral particles they recombine and emit photons in the process, causing <a href="/wiki/Airglow" title="Airglow">airglow</a>. The degree of ionization is sufficiently large to allow a constant emission of radiation even during the night when the upper atmosphere is in the Earth\'s shadow. Lower in the atmosphere all of the solar photons with energies above the ionization potential of N<sub>2</sub> and O<sub>2</sub> have already been absorbed by the higher layers and thus no appreciable ionization occurs.\n</p><p>Apart from emitting light, the sky also scatters incoming light, primarily from distant stars and the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a>, but also the <a href="/wiki/Zodiacal_light" title="Zodiacal light">zodiacal light</a>, sunlight that is reflected and backscattered from interplanetary dust particles.\n</p><p>The amount of airglow and zodiacal light is quite variable (depending, amongst other things on sunspot activity and the <a href="/wiki/Solar_cycle" title="Solar cycle">Solar cycle</a>) but given optimal conditions the darkest possible sky has a brightness of about 22 magnitude/square arcsecond. If a full moon is present, the <a href="/wiki/Sky_brightness" title="Sky brightness">sky brightness</a> increases to about 18 magnitude/sq. arcsecond depending on local atmospheric transparency, 40 times brighter than the darkest sky. In densely populated areas a sky brightness of 17 magnitude/sq. arcsecond is not uncommon, or as much as 100 times brighter than is natural.\n</p><p>To precisely measure how bright the sky gets, night time satellite imagery of the earth is used as raw input for the number and intensity of light sources. These are put into a physical model<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> of scattering due to air molecules and aerosoles to calculate cumulative sky brightness. Maps that show the enhanced sky brightness have been prepared for the entire world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Inspection of the area surrounding Madrid reveals that the effects of light pollution caused by a single large conglomeration can be felt up to 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) away from the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWA_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWA-28">[28]</a></sup>\nGlobal effects of light pollution are also made obvious. The entire area consisting of southern England, Netherlands, Belgium, west Germany, and northern France have a sky brightness of at least 2 to 4 times above normal (see above right). The only places in continental Europe where the sky can attain its natural darkness are in northern Scandinavia and in islands far from the continent.\n</p><p>In North America the situation is comparable. There is a significant problem with light pollution ranging from the Canadian Maritime Provinces to the American Southwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWA_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWA-28">[28]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Dark-Sky_Association" title="International Dark-Sky Association">International Dark-Sky Association</a> works to designate areas that have high quality night skies. These areas are supported by communities and organizations that are dedicated to reducing light pollution (e.g.<a href="/wiki/Dark-sky_preserve" title="Dark-sky preserve">Dark-sky preserve</a>). The <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_Sounds_and_Night_Skies_Division" title="Natural Sounds and Night Skies Division">Natural Sounds and Night Skies Division</a> has measured night sky quality in national park units across the U.S. Sky quality in the U.S. ranges from pristine (<a href="/wiki/Capitol_Reef_National_Park" title="Capitol Reef National Park">Capitol Reef National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Bend_National_Park" title="Big Bend National Park">Big Bend National Park</a>) to severely degraded (<a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica_Mountains_National_Recreation_Area" title="Santa Monica Mountains National Recreation Area">Santa Monica Mountains National Recreation Area</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_National_Park" title="Biscayne National Park">Biscayne National Park</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The National Park Service Night Sky Program monitoring database is available online (2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Light_pollution_in_Hong_Kong" title="Light pollution in Hong Kong">Light pollution in Hong Kong</a> was declared the \'worst on the planet\' in March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2016, it was estimated that one third of the world\'s population could no longer see the Milky Way, including 80% of Americans and 60% of Europeans. <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> was found to be the most light-polluted country in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-limitednight_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-limitednight-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWA_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-NWA-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="21600" data-file-width="43200" decoding="async" height="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/800px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/1200px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/1600px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A worldwide cloud-free mosaic from the <a href="/wiki/Suomi_NPP" title="Suomi NPP">Suomi NPP</a> satellite, showing the extent of visible lights in 2016. The effects of light pollution &#8211; especially <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a> &#8211; spread far beyond the light sources visible here.</div></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequences">Consequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Consequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_human_health_and_psychology">Effects on human health and psychology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Effects on human health and psychology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over-illumination" title="Over-illumination">Over-illumination</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecological_light_pollution" title="Ecological light pollution">Ecological light pollution</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2745" data-file-width="4213" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG/220px-Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG/330px-Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG/440px-Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lichtverschmutzung_in_Kastelruth.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Streetlights in the skiing resort <a href="/wiki/Kastelruth" title="Kastelruth">Kastelruth</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Tyrol" title="South Tyrol">South Tyrol</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Medical research on the effects of excessive light on the human body suggests that a variety of adverse health effects may be caused by light pollution or excessive light exposure, and some lighting design textbooks<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> use human health as an explicit criterion for proper interior lighting. Health effects of over-illumination or improper spectral composition of light may include: increased headache incidence, worker <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatigue_(physical)" title="Fatigue (physical)">fatigue</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stress_(medicine)" title="Stress (medicine)">medically defined stress</a>, decrease in <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">sexual</a> function and increase in anxiety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burks_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burks-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cambridge_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cambridge-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pijnenburg_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pijnenburg-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knez_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Knez-37">[37]</a></sup> Likewise, animal models have been studied demonstrating unavoidable light to produce adverse effect on mood and anxiety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadrodents_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadrodents-38">[38]</a></sup> For those who need to be awake at night, light at night also has an acute effect on alertness and mood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, "shift work that involves circadian disruption" was listed as a probable carcinogen by the World Health Organization\'s International Agency for Research on Cancer. (IARC Press release No. 180).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Multiple studies have documented a correlation between night shift work and the increased incidence of breast and prostate cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> One study which examined the link between exposure to artificial light at night (ALAN) and levels of <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a> in South Korea found that regions which had the highest levels of ALAN reported the highest number of cases of breast cancer.  Seoul, which had the highest levels of light pollution, had 34.4% more cases of breast cancer than Ganwon-do, which had the lowest levels of light pollution. This suggested a high correlation between ALAN and the prevalence of breast cancer.It was also found that there was no correlation between other types of cancer such as cervical or lung cancer and ALAN levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A more recent discussion (2009), written by Professor Steven Lockley, Harvard Medical School, can be found in the CfDS handbook "Blinded by the Light?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Chapter 4, "Human health implications of light pollution" states that "... light intrusion, even if dim, is likely to have measurable effects on sleep disruption and melatonin suppression. Even if these effects are relatively small from night to night, continuous chronic circadian, sleep and hormonal disruption may have longer-term health risks". The New York Academy of Sciences hosted a meeting in 2009 on Circadian Disruption and Cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Red light suppresses melatonin the least.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uchc_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-uchc-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2009, the <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">American Medical Association</a> developed a policy in support of control of light pollution. News about the decision emphasized <a href="/wiki/Glare_(vision)" title="Glare (vision)">glare</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> hazard leading to unsafe driving conditions. Especially in the elderly, glare produces loss of contrast, obscuring night vision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MottaJune09_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-MottaJune09-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disruption_of_ecosystems">Disruption of ecosystems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Disruption of ecosystems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecological_light_pollution" title="Ecological light pollution">Ecological light pollution</a></div>\n<p>When artificial light affects organisms and ecosystems it is called <a href="/wiki/Ecological_light_pollution" title="Ecological light pollution">ecological light pollution</a>. While light at night can be beneficial, neutral, or damaging for individual <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, its presence invariably disturbs ecosystems. For example, some species of spiders avoid lit areas, while other species are happy to build their <a href="/wiki/Spider_web" title="Spider web">spider web</a> directly on a lamp post. Since lamp posts attract many flying insects, the spiders that don\'t mind light gain an advantage over the spiders that avoid it. This is a simple example of the way in which species frequencies and food webs can be disturbed by the introduction of light at night.\n</p><p>Light pollution poses a serious threat in particular to <a href="/wiki/Nocturnality" title="Nocturnality">nocturnal</a> wildlife, having negative impacts on plant and animal physiology. It can confuse <a href="/wiki/Animal_navigation" title="Animal navigation">animal navigation</a>, alter competitive interactions, change predator-prey relations, and cause physiological harm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry08_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perry08-52">[52]</a></sup> The rhythm of life is orchestrated by the natural diurnal patterns of light and dark, so disruption to these patterns impacts the ecological dynamics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Studies suggest that light pollution around lakes prevents zooplankton, such as <a href="/wiki/Daphnia" title="Daphnia">Daphnia</a>, from eating surface <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>, causing <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">algal blooms</a> that can kill off the lakes\' plants and lower water quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Light pollution may also affect ecosystems in other ways. For example, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lepidopterist" title="Lepidopterist">lepidopterists</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entomologist" title="Entomologist">entomologists</a> have documented that nighttime light may interfere with the ability of moths and other nocturnal insects to navigate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Night-blooming flowers that depend on moths for <a href="/wiki/Pollination" title="Pollination">pollination</a> may be affected by night lighting, as there is no replacement <a href="/wiki/Pollinator" title="Pollinator">pollinator</a> that would not be affected by the artificial light. This can lead to species decline of plants that are unable to reproduce, and change an area\'s longterm <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Among nocturnal insects, <a href="/wiki/Firefly" title="Firefly">fireflies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Beetle" title="Beetle">Coleoptera</a>: Lampyridae, Phengodidae and Elateridae) are especially interesting study objects for light pollution, once they depend on their own light to reproduce and, consequently, are very sensitive to environmental levels of light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>  In 2015 it was shown and quantified for the first time the negative effects of direct illumination on fireflies, in a study that monitored populations over four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-60">[60]</a></sup> Fireflies are charismatic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> (which is a rare quality among insects) and are easily spotted by nonexperts, providing thus good <a href="/wiki/Flagship_species" title="Flagship species">flagship species</a> to attract public attention;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-60">[60]</a></sup> good investigation models for the effects of light on nocturnal wildlife;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-60">[60]</a></sup> and finally, due to their sensibility and rapid response to environmental changes, good <a href="/wiki/Bioindicator" title="Bioindicator">bioindicators</a> for artificial night lighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Massive insect declines have been suggested as being at least partially mediated by artificial lights at night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg/220px-Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg/330px-Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg/440px-Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scorpion_in_arizona.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A scorpion found in the San Tan mountains not accustomed to lights of the city hides under rocks from headlamps.  These nocturnal animals are very susceptible to light and its effects.</div></div></div>\n<p>A 2009 study<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PolarizedLightEnv_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-PolarizedLightEnv-64">[64]</a></sup> also suggests deleterious impacts on animals and ecosystems because of perturbation of polarized light or artificial polarization of light (even during the day, because direction of natural polarization of sun light and its reflection is a source of information for a lot of animals). This form of pollution is named <a href="/wiki/Polarized_light_pollution" title="Polarized light pollution">polarized light pollution</a> (PLP). Unnatural polarized light sources can trigger maladaptive behaviors in polarization-sensitive taxa and alter ecological interactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PolarizedLightEnv_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-PolarizedLightEnv-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lights on tall structures can disorient migrating birds. Estimates by the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service of the number of birds killed after being attracted to tall towers range from 4 to 5 million per year to an order of magnitude higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The Fatal Light Awareness Program (FLAP) works with building owners in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada and other cities to reduce mortality of birds by turning out lights during migration periods.\n</p><p>Similar disorientation has also been noted for bird species migrating close to offshore production and drilling facilities. Studies carried out by Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij b.v. (NAM) and Shell have led to development and trial of new lighting technologies in the North Sea. In early 2007, the lights were installed on the Shell production platform L15. The experiment proved a great success since the number of birds circling the platform declined by 50 to 90%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">Sea turtle</a> hatchlings emerging from nests on beaches are another casualty of light pollution. It is a common misconception that hatchling sea turtles are attracted to the moon. Rather, they find the ocean by moving away from the dark silhouette of dunes and their vegetation, a behavior with which artificial lights interfere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The breeding activity and reproductive phenology of toads, however, are cued by moonlight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Juvenile seabirds may also be disoriented by lights as they leave their nests and fly out to sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Amphibians and reptiles are also affected by light pollution. Introduced light sources during normally dark periods can disrupt levels of melatonin production. Melatonin is a hormone that regulates photoperiodic physiology and behaviour. Some species of frogs and salamanders utilize a light-dependent "compass" to orient their migratory behaviour to breeding sites. Introduced light can also cause developmental irregularities, such as retinal damage, reduced juvenile growth, premature metamorphosis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> reduced sperm production, and genetic mutation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry08_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perry08-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2009, the 9th European Dark-Sky Symposium in Armagh, Northern Ireland had a session on the environmental effects of light at night (LAN). It dealt with bats, turtles, the "hidden" harms of LAN, and many other topics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The environmental effects of LAN were mentioned as early as 1897, in a <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> article. The following is an excerpt from that article, called "Electricity and English songbirds":\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>An English journal has become alarmed at the relation of electricity to songbirds, which it maintains is closer than that of cats and fodder crops. How many of us, it asks, foresee that electricity may extirpate the songbird?...With the exception of the finches, all the English songbirds may be said to be insectivorous, and their diet consists chiefly of vast numbers of very small insects which they collect from the grass and herbs before the dew is dry. As the electric light is finding its way for street illumination into the country parts of England, these poor winged atoms are slain by thousands at each light every warm summer evening....The fear is expressed, that when England is lighted from one end to the other with electricity the song birds will die out from the failure of their food supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_astronomy">Effect on astronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Effect on astronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22" rel="nofollow">"Light pollution"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Light+pollution%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Light+pollution%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2008</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1012" data-file-width="1380" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg/220px-Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg/330px-Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg/440px-Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Light_pollution_It%27s_not_pretty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The constellation <a href="/wiki/Orion_(constellation)" title="Orion (constellation)">Orion</a>, imaged at left from dark skies, and at right from within the Provo/Orem, Utah metropolitan area.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">Astronomy</a> is very sensitive to light pollution. The <a href="/wiki/Night_sky" title="Night sky">night sky</a> viewed from a city bears no resemblance to what can be seen from dark skies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">Skyglow</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Light_scattering_by_particles" title="Light scattering by particles">scattering of light</a> in the atmosphere at night) reduces the contrast between stars and <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxies</a> and the sky itself, making it much harder to see fainter <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_object" title="Astronomical object">objects</a>. This is one factor that has caused newer <a href="/wiki/Telescope" title="Telescope">telescopes</a> to be built in increasingly remote areas.\n</p><p>Some astronomers use narrow-band "<a href="/wiki/Astronomical_filter" title="Astronomical filter">nebula filters</a>", which only allow specific wavelengths of light commonly seen in <a href="/wiki/Nebula" title="Nebula">nebulae</a>, or broad-band "light pollution filters", which are designed to reduce (but not eliminate) the effects of light pollution by <a href="/wiki/Optical_filter" title="Optical filter">filtering</a> out <a href="/wiki/Spectral_line" title="Spectral line">spectral lines</a> commonly emitted by <a href="/wiki/Sodium-vapor_lamp" title="Sodium-vapor lamp">sodium</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Mercury-vapor_lamp" title="Mercury-vapor lamp">mercury-vapor lamps</a>, thus enhancing contrast and improving the view of dim objects such as galaxies and nebulae.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Unfortunately, these light pollution reduction (LPR) filters are not a cure for light pollution. LPR filters reduce the brightness of the object under study and this limits the use of higher magnifications. LPR filters work by blocking light of certain wavelengths, which alters the color of the object, often creating a pronounced green cast. Furthermore, LPR filters only work on certain object types (mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emission_nebulae" title="Emission nebulae">emission nebulae</a>) and are of little use on galaxies and stars. No filter can match the effectiveness of a dark sky for visual or <a href="/wiki/Photographic_filter" title="Photographic filter">photographic</a> purposes.\n</p><p>Light pollution affects the visibility of <a href="/wiki/Deep-sky_object" title="Deep-sky object">diffuse sky objects</a> like nebulae and galaxies more than stars, due to their low surface brightness. Most such objects are rendered invisible in heavily light-polluted skies above major cities. A simple method for estimating the darkness of a location is to look for the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a>, which from truly dark skies appears bright enough to cast a shadow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5044" data-file-width="8337" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg/220px-Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg/330px-Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg/440px-Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Milky_Way_Shines_over_Snowy_La_Silla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outskirts of the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a>, far from the light-polluted cities of northern Chile, the skies are pitch-black after sunset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to skyglow, light trespass can impact observations when artificial light directly enters the tube of the telescope and is reflected from non-optical surfaces until it eventually reaches the <a href="/wiki/Eyepiece" title="Eyepiece">eyepiece</a>. This direct form of light pollution causes a glow across the <a href="/wiki/Field_of_view" title="Field of view">field of view</a>, which reduces contrast. Light trespass also makes it hard for a visual observer to become sufficiently adapted to the dark. The usual measures to reduce this glare, if reducing the light directly is not an option, include <a href="/wiki/Flocking_(texture)" title="Flocking (texture)">flocking</a> the telescope tube and accessories to reduce reflection, and putting a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Light_shield&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Light shield (page does not exist)">light shield</a> (also usable as a <a href="/wiki/Dew_shield" title="Dew shield">dew shield</a>) on the telescope to reduce light entering from angles other than those near the target. Under these conditions, some astronomers prefer to observe under a black cloth to ensure maximum <a href="/wiki/Adaptation_(eye)" title="Adaptation (eye)">adaptation</a> to the dark.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increase_in_atmospheric_pollution">Increase in atmospheric pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Increase in atmospheric pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A study presented at the <a href="/wiki/American_Geophysical_Union" title="American Geophysical Union">American Geophysical Union</a> meeting in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> found that light pollution destroys <a href="/wiki/Nitrate" title="Nitrate">nitrate</a> <a href="/wiki/Radical_(chemistry)" title="Radical (chemistry)">radicals</a> thus preventing the normal night time reduction of atmospheric smog produced by fumes emitted from cars and factories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The study was presented by Harald Stark from the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reduction_of_natural_sky_polarization">Reduction of natural sky polarization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reduction of natural sky polarization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="1136" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg/220px-Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg/330px-Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg/440px-Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Effect_of_light_pollution_on_sky_polarization.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Light pollution is mostly unpolarized, and its addition to moonlight results in a decreased polarization signal.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the night, the polarization of the moonlit sky is very strongly reduced in the presence of <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban</a> light pollution, because scattered urban light is not strongly polarized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Polarized moonlight can\'t be seen by humans, but is believed to be used by many animals for navigation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reduction">Reduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LED_Droplight.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LED_Droplight.JPG/220px-LED_Droplight.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LED_Droplight.JPG/330px-LED_Droplight.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LED_Droplight.JPG/440px-LED_Droplight.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LED_Droplight.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This kind of LED droplight could reduce unnecessary light pollution in building interiors</div></div></div>\n<p>Reducing light pollution implies many things, such as reducing sky glow, reducing glare, reducing light trespass, and reducing clutter. The method for best reducing light pollution, therefore, depends on exactly what the problem is in any given instance. Possible solutions include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Utilizing light sources of minimum intensity necessary to accomplish the light\'s purpose.</li>\n<li>Turning lights off using a timer or occupancy sensor or manually when not needed.</li>\n<li>Improving lighting fixtures, so that they direct their light more accurately towards where it is needed, and with fewer side effects.</li>\n<li>Adjusting the <i>type</i> of lights used, so that the light waves emitted are those that are less likely to cause severe light pollution problems. Mercury, metal halide and above all first generation of blue-light LED road luminaires are much more polluting than sodium lamps: Earth\'s atmosphere scatters and transmits blue light better than yellow or red light. It is a common experience observing "glare" and "fog" around and below LED road luminaires as soon as air humidity increases, while orange sodium lamp luminaires are less prone to showing this phenomenon.</li>\n<li>Evaluating existing lighting plans, and re-designing some or all of the plans depending on whether existing light is actually needed.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Improving_lighting_fixtures">Improving lighting fixtures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Improving lighting fixtures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22" rel="nofollow">"Light pollution"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Light+pollution%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Light+pollution%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Light+pollution%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2010</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="598" data-file-width="789" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/220px-Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/330px-Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/440px-Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flat-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i>flat-lens cobra luminaire</i>, which is a full-cutoff fixture, is very effective in reducing light pollution. It ensures that light is only directed below the horizontal, which means less light is wasted through directing it outwards and upwards.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="598" data-file-width="789" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/220px-Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/330px-Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg/440px-Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drop-lens_cobra_luminaire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This <i>drop-lens cobra luminaire</i> allows light to escape sideways and upwards, where it may cause problems.</div></div></div>\n<p>The use of <i>full cutoff</i> lighting fixtures, as much as possible, is advocated by most campaigners for the reduction of light pollution. It is also commonly recommended that lights be spaced appropriately for maximum efficiency, and that number of luminaires being used as well as the wattage of each luminaire match the needs of the particular application (based on local lighting design standards).\n</p><p>Full cutoff fixtures first became available in 1959 with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>\'s M100 fixture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AM-Feb2009-57_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-AM-Feb2009-57-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A full cutoff fixture, when correctly installed, reduces the chance for light to escape above the plane of the horizontal. Light released above the horizontal may sometimes be lighting an intended target, but often serves no purpose. When it enters into the atmosphere, light contributes to sky glow. Some governments and organizations are now considering, or have already implemented, full cutoff fixtures in street lamps and stadium lighting.\n</p><p>The use of full cutoff fixtures help to reduce sky glow by preventing light from escaping above the horizontal. Full cutoff typically reduces the visibility of the lamp and reflector within a luminaire, so the effects of glare are also reduced. Campaigners also commonly argue that full cutoff fixtures are more efficient than other fixtures, since light that would otherwise have escaped into the atmosphere may instead be directed towards the ground. However, full cutoff fixtures may also trap more light in the fixture than other types of luminaires, corresponding to lower luminaire efficiency, suggesting a re-design of some luminaires may be necessary.\n</p><p>The use of full cutoff fixtures can allow for lower wattage lamps to be used in the fixtures, producing the same or sometimes a better effect, due to being more carefully controlled. In every lighting system, some sky glow also results from light reflected from the ground. This reflection can be reduced, however, by being careful to use only the lowest wattage necessary for the lamp, and setting spacing between lights appropriately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Assuring luminaire setback is greater than 90&#176; from highly reflective surfaces also diminishes reflectance.\n</p><p>A common criticism of full cutoff lighting fixtures is that they are sometimes not as aesthetically pleasing to look at. This is most likely because historically there has not been a large market specifically for full cutoff fixtures, and because people typically like to see the source of illumination. Due to the specificity with their direction of light, full cutoff fixtures sometimes also require expertise to install for maximum effect.\n</p><p>The effectiveness of using full cutoff roadway lights to combat light pollution has also been called into question. According to design investigations, luminaires with full cutoff distributions (as opposed to <i>cutoff</i> or <i>semi cutoff</i>, compared here<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>) have to be closer together to meet the same light level, uniformity and glare requirements specified by the <a href="/wiki/Illuminating_Engineering_Society_of_North_America" title="Illuminating Engineering Society of North America">IESNA</a>. These simulations optimized the height and spacing of the lights while constraining the overall design to meet the IESNA requirements, and then compared total uplight and energy consumption of different luminaire designs and powers.
