Cutoff designs performed better than full cutoff designs, and semi-cutoff performed better than either cutoff or full cutoff. This indicates that, in roadway installations, over-illumination or poor uniformity produced by full cutoff fixtures may be more detrimental than direct uplight created by fewer cutoff or semi-cutoff fixtures. Therefore, the overall performance of existing systems could be improved more by reducing the number of luminaires than by switching to full cutoff designs.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg/220px-110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg/330px-110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg/440px-110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:110101_LightPollution_Italian_Regional_bills_specs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The majority of Italian regions require "zero upward light", which usually implies use of overall full cut-off lamps for new luminaires, but violations are common.</div></div></div>\n<p>However, using the definition of "light pollution" from some Italian regional bills (i.e., "every irradiance of artificial light outside competence areas and particularly upward the sky") only full cutoff design prevents light pollution. The Italian <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a> region, where only full cutoff design is allowed (Lombardy act no. 17/2000, promoted by <a href="/wiki/CieloBuio" title="CieloBuio">Cielobuio-coordination for the protection of the night sky</a>), in 2007 had the lowest per capita energy consumption for public lighting in Italy. The same legislation also imposes a minimum distance between street lamps of about four times their height, so full cut off street lamps are the best solution to reduce both light pollution and electrical power usage.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjusting_types_of_light_sources">Adjusting types of light sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Adjusting types of light sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several different types of light sources exist, each having different properties that affect their appropriateness for certain tasks, particularly efficiency and spectral power distribution. It is often the case that inappropriate light sources have been selected for a task, either due to ignorance or because more sophisticated light sources were unavailable at the time of installation. Therefore, badly chosen light sources often contribute unnecessarily to light pollution and energy waste. By re-assessing and changing the light sources used, it is often possible to reduce energy use and pollutive effects while simultaneously greatly improving efficiency and visibility.\n</p><p>Some types of light sources are listed in order of energy efficiency in the table below (figures are approximate maintained values), and include relative visual skyglow impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-luginbuhl2014_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-luginbuhl2014-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aube2013_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-aube2013-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:60%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Type of light source\n</th>\n<th>Color\n</th>\n<th>Luminous efficacy<br/>(in <a href="/wiki/Lumen_(unit)" title="Lumen (unit)">lumens</a> per <a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">watt</a>)\n</th>\n<th>Sky glow impact<br/>(relative to LPS)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/LED_street_light" title="LED street light">LED street light</a> (white)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fcfcff;">warm-white to cool-white\n</td>\n<td>120\n</td>\n<td>4&#8211;8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sodium_vapor_lamp#Low_pressure_sodium" title="Sodium vapor lamp">Low Pressure Sodium</a> (LPS/SOX)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff04f;">yellow/amber\n</td>\n<td>110\n</td>\n<td>1.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sodium_vapor_lamp#High_pressure_sodium" title="Sodium vapor lamp">High Pressure Sodium</a> (HPS/SON)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ffdc9f;">pink/amber-white\n</td>\n<td>90\n</td>\n<td>2.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_halide_lamp" title="Metal halide lamp">Metal Halide</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fcfcff;">warm-white to cool-white\n</td>\n<td>70\n</td>\n<td>4&#8211;8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">Incandescent</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ffffdf;">yellow/white\n</td>\n<td>8&#8211;25\n</td>\n<td>1.1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Many astronomers request that nearby communities use low pressure sodium lights or amber <a href="/wiki/Aluminium_gallium_indium_phosphide" title="Aluminium gallium indium phosphide">Aluminium gallium indium phosphide</a> LED as much as possible, because the principal wavelength emitted is comparably easy to work around or in rare cases filter out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The low cost of operating sodium lights is another feature. In 1980, for example, <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, replaced all street lamps with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_sodium_lamp" title="Low pressure sodium lamp">low pressure sodium lamps</a>, whose light is easier for nearby <a href="/wiki/Lick_Observatory" title="Lick Observatory">Lick Observatory</a> to filter out. Similar programs are now in place in <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. Such yellow light sources also have significantly less visual <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a> impact,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdsc-lslp_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-fdsc-lslp-92">[92]</a></sup> so reduce visual sky brightness and improve star visibility for everyone.\n</p><p>Disadvantages of low pressure sodium lighting are that fixtures must usually be larger than competing fixtures, and that color cannot be distinguished, due to its emitting principally a single wavelength of light (see <a href="/wiki/Security_lighting" title="Security lighting">security lighting</a>). Due to the substantial size of the lamp, particularly in higher wattages such as 135 W and 180 W, control of light emissions from low pressure sodium luminaires is more difficult. For applications requiring more precise direction of light (such as narrow roadways) the native lamp efficacy advantage of this lamp type is decreased and may be entirely lost compared to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sodium_vapor_lamp" title="Sodium vapor lamp">high pressure sodium lamps</a>. Allegations that this also leads to higher amounts of light pollution from luminaires running these lamps arise principally because of older luminaires with poor shielding, still widely in use in the UK and in some other locations. Modern low-pressure sodium fixtures with better optics and full shielding, and the decreased <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a> impacts of yellow light preserve the luminous efficacy advantage of low-pressure sodium and result in most cases is less energy consumption and less visible light pollution. Unfortunately, due to continued lack of accurate information,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> many lighting professionals continue to disparage low-pressure sodium, contributing to its decreased acceptance and specification in lighting standards and therefore its use. Another disadvantage of low-pressure sodium lamps is that some people find the characteristic yellow light very displeasing aesthetically.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This often-repeated claim needs documentation (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Because of the increased sensitivity of the human eye to blue and green wavelengths when viewing low-luminances (the <a href="/wiki/Purkinje_effect" title="Purkinje effect">Purkinje effect</a>) in the night sky, different sources produce dramatically different amounts of visible <a href="/wiki/Skyglow" title="Skyglow">skyglow</a> from the same amount of light sent into the atmosphere.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Re-designing_lighting_plans">Re-designing lighting plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Re-designing lighting plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In some cases, evaluation of existing plans has determined that more efficient lighting plans are possible. For instance, light pollution can be reduced by turning off unneeded outdoor lights, and only lighting stadiums when there are people inside. Timers are especially valuable for this purpose. One of the world\'s first coordinated <i>legislative</i> efforts to reduce the adverse effect of this pollution on the environment began in <a href="/wiki/Flagstaff,_Arizona" title="Flagstaff, Arizona">Flagstaff, Arizona</a>, in the U.S.  There, over three decades of ordinance development has taken place, with the full support of the population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> often with government support,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> with community advocates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and with the help of major local observatories,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Observatory_Flagstaff_Station" title="United States Naval Observatory Flagstaff Station">United States Naval Observatory Flagstaff Station</a>. Each component helps to educate, protect and enforce the imperatives to intelligently reduce detrimental light pollution.\n</p><p>One example of a lighting plan assessment can be seen in a report originally commissioned by the Office of the Deputy Prime Minister in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and now available through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_for_Communities_and_Local_Government" title="Department for Communities and Local Government">Department for Communities and Local Government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The report details a plan to be implemented throughout the UK, for designing lighting schemes in the countryside, with a particular focus on preserving the environment.\n</p><p>In another example, the city of <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a> has recently replaced most residential street lights with models that are comparably energy efficient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The motivation is primarily operation cost and environmental conservation. The costs of installation are expected to be regained through energy savings within six to seven years.\n</p><p>The Swiss Agency for Energy Efficiency (SAFE) uses a concept that promises to be of great use in the diagnosis and design of road lighting, "<i>consommation &#233;lectrique sp&#233;cifique</i> (<i>CES</i>)", which can be translated into English as "specific electric power consumption (SEC)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Thus, based on observed lighting levels in a wide range of Swiss towns, SAFE has defined target values for electric power consumption per metre for roads of various categories. Thus, SAFE currently recommends an SEC of 2 to 3 watts per meter for roads of less than 10 metre width (4 to 6 watts per metre for wider roads). Such a measure provides an easily applicable environmental protection constraint on conventional "norms", which usually are based on the recommendations of lighting manufacturing interests, who may not take into account environmental criteria. In view of ongoing progress in lighting technology, target SEC values will need to be periodically revised downwards.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1152" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg/220px-110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg/330px-110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg/440px-110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:110213_LED_vs_Sodium_vs_Mercury.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Crossroad in Alessandria, Italy: luminaires with mercury lamps are in the background, LED street lights in the middle, luminaires with high pressure sodium lamps are in the foreground.</div></div></div>\n<p>A newer method for predicting and measuring various aspects of light pollution was described in the journal Lighting Research Technology (September 2008). Scientists at <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>\'s Lighting Research Center have developed a comprehensive method called Outdoor Site-Lighting Performance (OSP), which allows users to quantify, and thus optimize, the performance of existing and planned lighting designs and applications to minimize excessive or obtrusive light leaving the boundaries of a property. OSP can be used by lighting engineers immediately, particularly for the investigation of glow and trespass (glare analyses are more complex to perform and current commercial software does not readily allow them), and can help users compare several lighting design alternatives for the same site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the effort to reduce light pollution, researchers have developed a "Unified System of Photometry," which is a way to measure how much or what kind of <a href="/wiki/Street_light" title="Street light">street lighting</a> is needed. The Unified System of Photometry allows light fixtures to be designed to reduce energy use while maintaining or improving perceptions of visibility, safety, and security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> There was a need to create a new system of light measurement at night because the biological way in which the eye&#8217;s rods and cones process light is different in nighttime conditions versus daytime conditions. Using this new system of photometry, results from recent studies have indicated that replacing traditional, yellowish, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_pressure_sodium" title="High pressure sodium">high-pressure sodium</a> (HPS) lights with "cool" white light sources, such as induction, <a href="/wiki/Fluorescent_lamp" title="Fluorescent lamp">fluorescent</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceramic_discharge_metal_halide_lamp" title="Ceramic discharge metal halide lamp">ceramic metal halide</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LED" title="LED">LEDs</a> can actually reduce the amount of electric power used for lighting while maintaining or improving visibility in nighttime conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Illumination" title="International Commission on Illumination">International Commission on Illumination</a>, also known as the CIE from its French title, la Commission Internationale de l\'Eclairage, will soon be releasing its own form of unified photometry for outdoor lighting.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_pollution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="metadata href="/wiki/Photosensitive_epilepsy" title="Photosensitive epilepsy">Photosensitive epilepsy</a></li></ul></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span
